## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: materials science & solid mechanics (thermo-mechanical constitutive modeling)
**Analysis**: The variables are stress (sigma) as a function of strain (epsilon) and temperature (T), which is characteristic of constitutive laws for solids where stiffness, yielding, and hardening/softening depend on temperature. Common relationships include linear/nonlinear elasticity, plasticity with temperature-dependent yield stress, and viscoelastic/creep-like temperature sensitivity captured via exponential or shift-factor forms.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Hooke’s law (isothermal linear elasticity): sigma = c0 * epsilon (small-strain elastic regime)
- Temperature-dependent modulus (linear thermoelastic stiffness): sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon (elastic modulus varies approximately linearly with temperature)
- Polynomial modulus in temperature: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T + c2 * T**2) * epsilon (smooth thermal softening/stiffening of elastic response)
- Nonlinear elastic (Landau-type expansion): sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**3 (moderate-strain hyperelastic-like nonlinearity)
- Thermal modulation of nonlinearity: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon + (c2 + c3 * T) * epsilon**3 (temperature affects both linear and nonlinear stiffness terms)
- Ramberg–Osgood-like relation (implicit, often fit in explicit rearranged form): epsilon = c0 * sigma + c1 * sigma**c2 (elastic + power-law plastic strain; can be inverted/approximated to model sigma(epsilon,T))
- Power-law hardening with thermal factor: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(c2 * T) (strain hardening with temperature-sensitive strength scale)
- Johnson–Cook-style separable form (structure): sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (c3 + c4 * T**c5) (plastic flow stress with strain hardening and thermal softening factor)
- Thermal softening via rational temperature factor: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) / (T + c3) (strength decreases with temperature over a range)
- Yield + hardening with smooth transition: sigma = c0 + c1 * log(c2 * epsilon + c3) (post-yield logarithmic hardening; often used empirically for metals/polymers)
- Exponential saturation hardening: sigma = c0 + c1 * (1 - exp(c2 * epsilon)) (hardening approaching an asymptote)
- Thermoelastic stress with thermal strain offset (structure): sigma = c0 * (epsilon - c1 * T) (stress from mechanical strain minus thermal expansion contribution)
- Eyring/activated flow inspired stress scale (empirical): sigma = c0 * asinh(c1 * epsilon) * exp(c2 * T) (captures nonlinear stress growth with strain and strong temperature sensitivity)
- Viscoelastic/creep surrogate with temperature-dependent compliance (static proxy): sigma = epsilon / (c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * T)) (effective modulus decreases with temperature via an activated compliance term)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Linear small-strain elasticity → sigma proportional to epsilon, with slope interpreted as an effective modulus that may depend on T.
- Thermal softening of stiffness/strength → multiplicative factors decreasing with T (e.g., (c0 + c1*T), 1/(T+c), exp(c*T) with negative c).
- Post-yield hardening → sigma increases sublinearly with epsilon (log(1+epsilon), epsilon**n with 0<n<1) or saturates toward an asymptote (1-exp(c*epsilon)).
- Strong curvature at moderate strains → inclusion of higher-order elastic terms (epsilon**3, epsilon**5) to capture nonlinear elasticity/hyperelasticity-like response.
- Separable hardening and thermal terms → product of a strain-only part and a temperature-only part, reflecting independent mechanisms (work hardening vs thermal activation).
- Thermal strain compensation → dependence on (epsilon - c*T), indicating stress-free expansion and residual/constraint-induced stress when thermal expansion is restrained.
- Activated mechanisms (creep/flow) → exponential dependence on T multiplying compliance or strength scale, often producing rapid changes over temperature.
- Smooth regime transitions (elastic→plastic) → use of logs, asinh/tanh, or exponential saturation to avoid sharp yield corners in sigma(epsilon,T).
